Istio’s powerful features provide a uniform and more efficient way to secure, connect, and monitor services. Istio is the path to load balancing, service-to-service authentication, and monitoring – with few or no service code changes.\\n18: \\n19: - For in-depth information about how to use Istio, visit [istio.io](https://istio.io)\\n20: - To ask questions and get assistance from our community, visit [GitHub Discussions](https://github.com/istio/istio/discussions)\\n21: - To learn how to participate in our overall community, visit [our community page](https://istio.io/about/community)\\n22: \\n23: In this README:\\n24: \\n25: - [Introduction](#introduction)\\n26: - [Repositories](#repositories)\\n27: - [Issue management](#issue-management)\\n28: \\n29: In addition, here are some other documents you may wish to read:\\n30: \\n31: - [Istio Community](https://github.com/istio/community#istio-community) - describes how to get involved and contribute to the Istio project\\n32: - [Istio Developer's Guide](https://github.com/istio/istio/wiki/Preparing-for-Development) - explains how to set up and use an Istio development environment\\n33: - [Project Conventions](https://github.com/istio/istio/wiki/Development-Conventions) - describes the conventions we use within the code base\\n34: - [Creating Fast and Lean Code](https://github.com/istio/istio/wiki/Writing-Fast-and-Lean-Code) - performance-oriented advice and guidelines for the code base\\n35: \\n36: You'll find many other useful documents on our [Wiki](https://github.com/istio/istio/wiki).\\n37: \\n38: ## Introduction\\n39: \\n40: [Istio](https://istio.io/latest/docs/concepts/what-is-istio/) is an open platform for providing a uniform way to [integrate\\n41: microservices](https://istio.io/latest/docs/examples/microservices-istio/), manage [traffic flow](https://istio.io/latest/docs/concepts/traffic-management/) across microservices, enforce policies\\n42: and aggregate telemetry data. Istio's control plane provides an abstraction\\n43: layer over the underlying cluster management platform, such as Kubernetes.\\n44: \\n45: Istio is composed of these components:\\n46: \\n47: - **Envoy** - Sidecar proxies per microservice to handle ingress/egress traffic\\n48:    between services in the cluster and from a service to external\\n49:    services. The proxies form a _secure microservice mesh_ providing a rich\\n50:    set of functions like discovery, rich layer-7 routing, circuit breakers,\\n51:    policy enforcement and telemetry recording/reporting\\n52:    functions.\\n53: \\n54:   > Note: The service mesh is not an overlay network. It\\n55:   > simplifies and enhances how microservices in an application talk to each\\n56:   > other over the network provided by the underlying platform.\\n57: \\n58: * **Ztunnel** - A lightweight data plane proxy written in Rust,\\n59:     used in Ambient mesh mode to provide secure connectivity and observability for workloads without sidecar proxies.\\n60: \\n61: - **Istiod** - The Istio control plane. It provides service discovery, configuration and certificate management.\\n62: \\n63: ## Repositories\\n64: \\n65: The Istio project is divided across a few GitHub repositories:\\n66: \\n67: - [istio/api](https://github.com/istio/api). This repository defines\\n68: component-level APIs and common configuration formats for the Istio platform.\\n69: \\n70: - [istio/community](https://github.com/istio/community). This repository contains\\n71: information on the Istio community, including the various documents that govern\\n72: the Istio open source project.\\n73: \\n74: - [istio/istio](README.md). This is the main code repository. It hosts Istio's\\n75: core components, install artifacts, and sample programs. It includes:\\n76: \\n77:     - [istioctl](istioctl/). This directory contains code for the\\n78: [_istioctl_](https://istio.io/latest/docs/reference/commands/istioctl/) command line utility.\\n79: \\n80:     - [pilot](pilot/). This directory\\n81: contains platform-specific code to populate the\\n82: [abstract service model](https://istio.io/docs/concepts/traffic-management/#pilot), dynamically reconfigure the proxies\\n83: when the application topology changes, as well as translate\\n84: [routing rules](https://istio.io/latest/docs/reference/config/networking/) into proxy specific configuration.\\n85: \\n86:     - [security](security/). This directory contains [security](https://istio.io/latest/docs/concepts/security/) related code.\\n87: \\n88: - [istio/proxy](https://github.com/istio/proxy). The Istio proxy contains\\n89: extensions to the [Envoy proxy](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy) (in the form of\\n90: Envoy filters) that support authentication, authorization, and telemetry collection.\\n91: \\n92: - [istio/ztunnel](https://github.com/istio/ztunnel). The repository contains the Rust implementation of the ztunnel\\n93: component of Ambient mesh.\\n94: \\n95: - [istio/client-go](https://github.com/istio/client-go). This repository defines\\n96:   auto-generated Kubernetes clients for interacting with Istio resources programmatically.\\n97: \\n98: > [!NOTE]\\n99: > Only the `istio/api` and `istio/client-go` repositories expose stable interfaces intended for direct usage as libraries.\\n100: \\n101: ## Issue management\\n102: \\n103: We use GitHub to track all of our bugs and feature requests. Each issue we track has a variety of metadata:\\n104: \\n105: - **Epic**. An epic represents a feature area for Istio as a whole. Epics are fairly broad in scope and are basically product-level things.\\n106: Each issue is ultimately part of an epic.\\n107: \\n108: - **Milestone**. Each issue is assigned a milestone. This is 0.1, 0.2, ..., or 'Nebulous Future'. The milestone indicates when we\\n109: think the issue should get addressed.\\n110: \\n111: - **Priority**. Each issue has a priority which is represented by the column in the [Prioritization](https://github.com/orgs/istio/projects/6) project. Priority can be one of\\n112: P0, P1, P2, or >P2. The priority indicates how important it is to address the issue within the milestone. P0 says that the\\n113: milestone cannot be considered achieved if the issue isn't resolved.\\n114: \\n115: ---\\n116: \\n117: <div align=\\\"center\\\">\\n118:     <picture>\\n119:       <source media=\\\"(prefers-color-scheme: dark)\\\" srcset=\\\"https://raw.githubusercontent.com/cncf/artwork/refs/heads/main/other/cncf/horizontal/color-whitetext/cncf-color-whitetext.svg\\\">\\n120:       <source media=\\\"(prefers-color-scheme: light)\\\" srcset=\\\"https://raw.githubusercontent.com/cncf/artwork/master/other/cncf/horizontal/color/cncf-color.svg\\\">\\n121:       <img width=\\\"300\\\" alt=\\\"Cloud Native Computing Foundation logo\\\" src=\\\"https://raw.githubusercontent.com/cncf/artwork/refs/heads/main/other/cncf/horizontal/color-whitetext/cncf-color-whitetext.svg\\\">\\n122:     </picture>\\n123:     <p>Istio is a <a href=\\\"https://cncf.io\\\">Cloud Native Computing Foundation</a> project.</p>\\n124: </div>\\n125: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-benchmarks/istio--f8af3cae@3a22a44f97d470ed898e4dfb3b17913cb295c7bf/-/blob/README.md\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"e82f3759-3937-4e3e-bae9-228ea45955c3","uuid":"29409761-0036-4330-9ab5-183d96b66877","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: # Istio\n2: \n3: [![CII Best Practices](https://bestpractices.coreinfrastructure.org/projects/1395/badge)](https://bestpractices.coreinfrastructure.org/projects/1395)\n4: [![Go Report Card](https://goreportcard.com/badge/github.com/istio/istio)](https://goreportcard.com/report/github.com/istio/istio)\n5: [![GoDoc](https://godoc.org/istio.io/istio?status.svg)](https://godoc.org/istio.io/istio)\n6: \n7: <a href=\"https://istio.io/\">\n8:     <picture>\n9:       <source media=\"(prefers-color-scheme: dark)\" srcset=\"https://raw.githubusercontent.com/cncf/artwork/refs/heads/main/projects/istio/icon/color/istio-icon-color.svg\">\n10:       <source media=\"(prefers-color-scheme: light)\" srcset=\"https://github.com/istio/istio/raw/master/logo/istio-bluelogo-whitebackground-unframed.svg\">\n11:       <img title=\"Istio\" height=\"100\" width=\"100\" alt=\"Istio logo\" src=\"https://github.com/istio/istio/raw/master/logo/istio-bluelogo-whitebackground-unframed.svg\">\n12:     </picture>\n13: </a>\n14: \n15: ---\n16: \n17: Istio is an open source service mesh that layers transparently onto existing distributed applications. Istio’s powerful features provide a uniform and more efficient way to secure, connect, and monitor services. Istio is the path to load balancing, service-to-service authentication, and monitoring – with few or no service code changes.\n18: \n19: - For in-depth information about how to use Istio, visit [istio.io](https://istio.io)\n20: - To ask questions and get assistance from our community, visit [GitHub Discussions](https://github.com/istio/istio/discussions)\n21: - To learn how to participate in our overall community, visit [our community page](https://istio.io/about/community)\n22: \n23: In this README:\n24: \n25: - [Introduction](#introduction)\n26: - [Repositories](#repositories)\n27: - [Issue management](#issue-management)\n28: \n29: In addition, here are some other documents you may wish to read:\n30: \n31: - [Istio Community](https://github.com/istio/community#istio-community) - describes how to get involved and contribute to the Istio project\n32: - [Istio Developer's Guide](https://github.com/istio/istio/wiki/Preparing-for-Development) - explains how to set up and use an Istio development environment\n33: - [Project Conventions](https://github.com/istio/istio/wiki/Development-Conventions) - describes the conventions we use within the code base\n34: - [Creating Fast and Lean Code](https://github.com/istio/istio/wiki/Writing-Fast-and-Lean-Code) - performance-oriented advice and guidelines for the code base\n35: \n36: You'll find many other useful documents on our [Wiki](https://github.com/istio/istio/wiki).\n37: \n38: ## Introduction\n39: \n40: [Istio](https://istio.io/latest/docs/concepts/what-is-istio/) is an open platform for providing a uniform way to [integrate\n41: microservices](https://istio.io/latest/docs/examples/microservices-istio/), manage [traffic flow](https://istio.io/latest/docs/concepts/traffic-management/) across microservices, enforce policies\n42: and aggregate telemetry data. Istio's control plane provides an abstraction\n43: layer over the underlying cluster management platform, such as Kubernetes.\n44: \n45: Istio is composed of these components:\n46: \n47: - **Envoy** - Sidecar proxies per microservice to handle ingress/egress traffic\n48:    between services in the cluster and from a service to external\n49:    services. The proxies form a _secure microservice mesh_ providing a rich\n50:    set of functions like discovery, rich layer-7 routing, circuit breakers,\n51:    policy enforcement and telemetry recording/reporting\n52:    functions.\n53: \n54:   > Note: The service mesh is not an overlay network. It\n55:   > simplifies and enhances how microservices in an application talk to each\n56:   > other over the network provided by the underlying platform.\n57: \n58: * **Ztunnel** - A lightweight data plane proxy written in Rust,\n59:     used in Ambient mesh mode to provide secure connectivity and observability for workloads without sidecar proxies.\n60: \n61: - **Istiod** - The Istio control plane. It provides service discovery, configuration and certificate management.\n62: \n63: ## Repositories\n64: \n65: The Istio project is divided across a few GitHub repositories:\n66: \n67: - [istio/api](https://github.com/istio/api). This repository defines\n68: component-level APIs and common configuration formats for the Istio platform.\n69: \n70: - [istio/community](https://github.com/istio/community). This repository contains\n71: information on the Istio community, including the various documents that govern\n72: the Istio open source project.\n73: \n74: - [istio/istio](README.md). This is the main code repository. It hosts Istio's\n75: core components, install artifacts, and sample programs. It includes:\n76: \n77:     - [istioctl](istioctl/). This directory contains code for the\n78: [_istioctl_](https://istio.io/latest/docs/reference/commands/istioctl/) command line utility.\n79: \n80:     - [pilot](pilot/). This directory\n81: contains platform-specific code to populate the\n82: [abstract service model](https://istio.io/docs/concepts/traffic-management/#pilot), dynamically reconfigure the proxies\n83: when the application topology changes, as well as translate\n84: [routing rules](https://istio.io/latest/docs/reference/config/networking/) into proxy specific configuration.\n85: \n86:     - [security](security/). This directory contains [security](https://istio.io/latest/docs/concepts/security/) related code.\n87: \n88: - [istio/proxy](https://github.com/istio/proxy). The Istio proxy contains\n89: extensions to the [Envoy proxy](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy) (in the form of\n90: Envoy filters) that support authentication, authorization, and telemetry collection.\n91: \n92: - [istio/ztunnel](https://github.com/istio/ztunnel). The repository contains the Rust implementation of the ztunnel\n93: component of Ambient mesh.\n94: \n95: - [istio/client-go](https://github.com/istio/client-go). This repository defines\n96:   auto-generated Kubernetes clients for interacting with Istio resources programmatically.\n97: \n98: > [!NOTE]\n99: > Only the `istio/api` and `istio/client-go` repositories expose stable interfaces intended for direct usage as libraries.\n100: \n101: ## Issue management\n102: \n103: We use GitHub to track all of our bugs and feature requests. Each issue we track has a variety of metadata:\n104: \n105: - **Epic**. An epic represents a feature area for Istio as a whole. Epics are fairly broad in scope and are basically product-level things.\n106: Each issue is ultimately part of an epic.\n107: \n108: - **Milestone**. Each issue is assigned a milestone. This is 0.1, 0.2, ..., or 'Nebulous Future'. The milestone indicates when we\n109: think the issue should get addressed.\n110: \n111: - **Priority**. Each issue has a priority which is represented by the column in the [Prioritization](https://github.com/orgs/istio/projects/6) project. Priority can be one of\n112: P0, P1, P2, or >P2. The priority indicates how important it is to address the issue within the milestone. P0 says that the\n113: milestone cannot be considered achieved if the issue isn't resolved.\n114: \n115: ---\n116: \n117: <div align=\"center\">\n118:     <picture>\n119:       <source media=\"(prefers-color-scheme: dark)\" srcset=\"https://raw.githubusercontent.com/cncf/artwork/refs/heads/main/other/cncf/horizontal/color-whitetext/cncf-color-whitetext.svg\">\n120:       <source media=\"(prefers-color-scheme: light)\" srcset=\"https://raw.githubusercontent.com/cncf/artwork/master/other/cncf/horizontal/color/cncf-color.svg\">\n121:       <img width=\"300\" alt=\"Cloud Native Computing Foundation logo\" src=\"https://raw.githubusercontent.com/cncf/artwork/refs/heads/main/other/cncf/horizontal/color-whitetext/cncf-color-whitetext.svg\">\n122:     </picture>\n123:     <p>Istio is a <a href=\"https://cncf.io\">Cloud Native Computing Foundation</a> project.</p>\n124: </div>\n125: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-benchmarks/istio--f8af3cae@3a22a44f97d470ed898e4dfb3b17913cb295c7bf/-/blob/README.md"}}}

If this number is less than InboundUpdates,\n89: \t// there are updates we have not yet processed.\n90: \t// Note: This does not mean that all proxies have received these configurations; it is strictly\n91: \t// the push context, which means that the next push to a proxy will receive this configuration.\n92: \tCommittedUpdates *atomic.Int64\n93: \n94: \t// pushChannel is the buffer used for debouncing.\n95: \t// after debouncing the pushRequest will be sent to pushQueue\n96: \tpushChannel chan *model.PushRequest\n97: \n98: \t// pushQueue is the buffer that used after debounce and before the real xds push.\n99: \tpushQueue *PushQueue\n100: \n101: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-benchmarks/istio--f8af3cae@3a22a44f97d470ed898e4dfb3b17913cb295c7bf/-/blob/pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go%3FL1-100"}}}

{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_016CmXnq3jsH1YTR2i9h33YA","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_016KhsJsWdZ7rFpzEiL97i9g","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Istio Control Plane Developer Onboarding Guide\n\nWelcome to Istio! This guide will help you understand the control plane architecture, set up your development environment, and make your first contribution.\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [Build Prerequisites](#build-prerequisites)\n2. [Architecture Overview](#architecture-overview)\n3. [First Contribution Workflow](#first-contribution-workflow)\n4. [Debugging and Development](#debugging-and-development)\n5. [Key Resources](#key-resources)\n\n---\n\n## Build Prerequisites\n\n### System Requirements\n\n**Go Version**: 1.25.0 or later (as specified in `go.mod`)\n\nVerify your Go installation:\n```bash\ngo version\n```\n\n### Environment Setup\n\n**Clone the Repository** (with all submodules):\n```bash\ngit clone --recurse-submodules https://github.com/istio/istio.git\ncd istio\n```\n\nIf you've already cloned without submodules, initialize them:\n```bash\ngit submodule update --init --recursive\n```\n\n### Build System\n\nIstio uses a Makefile-based build system with two modes:\n\n#### Option 1: Local Build (Recommended for Development)\n\n```bash\nmake build\n```\n\nThis compiles binaries directly on your machine. You'll need:\n- Go toolchain\n- Standard build tools (gcc, make)\n\n#### Option 2: Containerized Build\n\nFor a completely isolated environment (fewer system dependencies):\n```bash\nBUILD_WITH_CONTAINER=1 make build\n```\n\nThis uses Docker to build everything in a consistent container environment. Requires Docker to be installed.\n\n### Core Binaries\n\nThe main control plane binaries built by the system are:\n\n- **`pilot-discovery`**: The core Istio discovery server, handles xDS protocol and configuration distribution\n  - Location: `./pilot/cmd/pilot-discovery`\n  - Built target: `$GOBIN/pilot-discovery`\n\n- **`pilot-agent`**: Sidecar agent that runs in each Envoy pod, manages local configuration\n  - Location: `./pilot/cmd/pilot-agent`\n  - Built target: `$GOBIN/pilot-agent`\n\n- **`istioctl`**: CLI tool for debugging and managing Istio\n  - Location: `./istioctl/cmd/istioctl`\n  - Built target: `$GOBIN/istioctl`\n\nTo build individual binaries:\n```bash\nmake pilot-discovery\nmake pilot-agent\nmake istioctl\n```\n\n### Running Tests\n\n**Unit Tests with Race Detection** (recommended):\n```bash\nmake test\n```\n\nThis runs: `go test ./... -race -tags=assert`\n\n**Run Tests for Specific Packages**:\n```bash\n# Test only the pilot package\nPKG=./pilot/... make test\n\n# Test only xDS discovery server\nPKG=./pilot/pkg/xds/... make test\n```\n\n**Run Benchmarks**:\n```bash\nmake benchtest\n```\n\n### Pre-commit Checks\n\nBefore submitting a PR, run the complete pre-commit pipeline:\n```bash\nmake precommit\n```\n\nThis runs:\n- `make fmt` - Code formatting (gofmt, goimports)\n- `make lint` - Linting (go vet, copyright banners, scripts, YAML, markdown, etc.)\n- `make tidy-go` - Dependency management\n\n**Just formatting**:\n```bash\nmake format\n```\n\n---\n\n## Architecture Overview\n\n### Control Plane Components\n\nIstio's control plane (istiod) is a single unified binary that merges three historical components:\n\n1. **Pilot** - Service discovery and traffic management\n   - Watches Kubernetes Services and ServiceEntry resources\n   - Generates xDS configuration for Envoy proxies\n   - Implements traffic policies (routing, load balancing, retries)\n\n2. **Citadel** - Certificate Authority and Identity Management\n   - Issues and manages mTLS certificates for workloads\n   - Provides certificate rotation and distribution\n   - Manages certificate revocation\n\n3. **Galley** - Configuration validation and distribution\n   - Validates Istio CRDs and Kubernetes resources\n   - Distributes validated configurations to other components\n\n### xDS Protocol: Configuration Distribution\n\nThe **xDS API** is the core protocol by which istiod pushes configuration to Envoy proxies. It consists of four main resource types:\n\n- **CDS** (Cluster Discovery Service): Defines upstream services as \"clusters\"\n  - Each cluster represents a service that traffic can be sent to\n  - Includes load balancing policies and health checks\n  - Generated by: `pilot/pkg/xds/cds.go`\n\n- **EDS** (Endpoint Discovery Service): Lists IP addresses for each cluster\n  - Provides the actual endpoints (pods) behind each service\n  - Updated when pods start/stop or change state\n  - Generated by: `pilot/pkg/xds/eds.go`\n\n- **LDS** (Listener Discovery Service): Defines listening sockets on the proxy\n  - Specifies ports and protocols the Envoy proxy should listen on\n  - Configures filter chains for different traffic types\n  - Generated by: `pilot/pkg/xds/lds.go`\n\n- **RDS** (Route Discovery Service): Defines routing rules\n  - Specifies how to route traffic between services\n  - Implements VirtualService, DestinationRule, and traffic policies\n  - Generated by: `pilot/pkg/xds/rds.go`\n\n### Data Flow: Service Discovery to xDS Push\n\nHere's the complete end-to-end flow when a new service is discovered:\n\n```\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ 1. SERVICE REGISTRATION                                         │\n│    Kubernetes API Server creates a Service object               │\n└────────────────────┬────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n                     │\n                     ▼\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ 2. SERVICE DISCOVERY                                            │\n│    ServiceRegistry (pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/)                │\n│    - KubeRegistry watches Kubernetes Services                  │\n│    - ServiceEntryRegistry watches ServiceEntry CRDs            │\n│    - AggregateRegistry combines multiple registries            │\n│                                                                 │\n│    Key files:                                                  │\n│    - serviceregistry/kube/controller/controller.go              │\n│    - serviceregistry/serviceentry/controller.go                │\n│    - serviceregistry/aggregate/controller.go                   │\n└────────────────────┬────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n                     │\n                     ▼\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ 3. CONFIGURATION UPDATE TRIGGER                                 │\n│    ServiceDiscovery emits event → PushRequest created           │\n│    Request queued in DiscoveryServer.pushChannel               │\n│                                                                 │\n│    Key files:                                                  │\n│    - xds/discovery.go (DiscoveryServer.push handler)           │\n│    - model/push.go (PushRequest/PushContext)                   │\n└────────────────────┬────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n                     │\n                     ▼\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ 4. DEBOUNCING & CONTEXT INITIALIZATION                         │\n│    Multiple events batched for efficiency                       │\n│    initPushContext() builds new model.PushContext with:        │\n│    - Current service registry state                            │\n│    - Mesh configuration                                        │\n│    - All defined VirtualServices and DestinationRules         │\n│    - Security policies                                         │\n│                                                                 │\n│    Key files:                                                  │\n│    - model/pushcontext.go (PushContext initialization)         │\n│    - xds/discovery.go:initPushContext()                       │\n└────────────────────┬────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n                     │\n                     ▼\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ 5. CONFIGURATION GENERATION                                     │\n│    For each connected proxy, generators build xDS resources:   │\n│                                                                 │\n│    CDS Generator (xds/cds.go)                                  │\n│    → Calls ConfigGenerator.BuildClusters()                     │\n│    → Creates Cluster resources for all services                │\n│                                                                 │\n│    EDS Generator (xds/eds.go)                                  │\n│    → Calls ConfigGenerator.BuildEndpoints()                    │\n│    → Creates ClusterLoadAssignment for each cluster            │\n│    → Reads from EndpointIndex (service discovery)              │\n│                                                                 │\n│    LDS Generator (xds/lds.go)                                  │\n│    → Calls ConfigGenerator.BuildListeners()                    │\n│    → Creates Listener resources on proxy's ports               │\n│                                                                 │\n│    RDS Generator (xds/rds.go)                                  │\n│    → Calls ConfigGenerator.BuildRoutes()                       │\n│    → Creates RouteConfiguration with VirtualService rules     │\n│                                                                 │\n│    Key files:                                                  │\n│    - pilot/pkg/networking/core/configgen.go (ConfigGenerator) │\n│    - pilot/pkg/xds/v3/ (xDS generators)                       │\n└────────────────────┬────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n                     │\n                     ▼\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ 6. XDS PUSH TO PROXIES                                          │\n│    DiscoveryServer.AdsPushAll() or AdsPush()                   │\n│    sends update via gRPC to all connected Envoy proxies        │\n│                                                                 │\n│    Protocols:                                                  │\n│    - ADS (Aggregated Discovery Service): Single gRPC stream    │\n│    - Delta xDS: Incremental updates                            │\n│                                                                 │\n│    Key files:                                                  │\n│    - xds/ads.go (ADS protocol)                                 │\n│    - xds/delta.go (Delta xDS)                                  │\n│    - xds/discovery.go (Push implementation)                    │\n└────────────────────┬────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n                     │\n                     ▼\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ 7. PROXY APPLICATION                                            │\n│    Envoy proxy receives xDS update                             │\n│    → Updates local routing configuration                       │\n│    → Applies new clusters, endpoints, listeners, routes        │\n│    → Traffic now flows according to new configuration          │\n└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n### Key Packages and Their Responsibilities\n\n#### `pilot/pkg/xds/` - xDS Protocol Implementation\n- **discovery.go**: Core DiscoveryServer that manages gRPC connections and pushes\n- **ads.go**: ADS (Aggregated Discovery Service) protocol handler\n- **delta.go**: Delta xDS incremental update handler\n- **cds.go, eds.go, lds.go, rds.go**: Individual xDS resource generators\n- **monitoring.go**: Metrics for push operations and timing\n\n**Entry point**: `DiscoveryServer` struct in discovery.go:64\n\n#### `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/` - Service Discovery\nMultiple registry implementations:\n- **kube/controller/**: Kubernetes service discovery (watches K8s API)\n- **serviceentry/**: ServiceEntry resource discovery\n- **aggregate/**: Combines multiple registries\n\n**Key interface**: `Instance` interface for service registries\n\n#### `pilot/pkg/bootstrap/` - Server Initialization\n- **server.go**: Main Server struct (line 105) that orchestrates istiod startup\n- **servicecontroller.go**: Initializes all service registries\n- **configcontroller.go**: Sets up configuration watchers for CRDs\n- **discovery.go**: Initializes xDS generators\n- **istio_ca.go**: Certificate Authority initialization\n- **mesh.go**: Mesh configuration loading\n\n#### `pilot/pkg/model/` - Core Data Models\n- **environment.go**: Global Environment with ServiceDiscovery, ConfigStore\n- **push.go**: PushContext and PushRequest (configuration version)\n- **proxy.go**: Proxy model representing an Envoy instance\n\n#### `pilot/pkg/networking/` - Configuration Generation\n- **core/configgen.go**: ConfigGenerator interface for building xDS resources\n- **core/v1alpha3/**: Legacy traffic management implementation\n- **security/authz/**: Authorization policy generation\n- **policy/**: Traffic policy implementation\n\n#### `security/pkg/` - Certificate Management\n- **pki/**: Private key infrastructure and CA operations\n- **server/ca/**: CA server for certificate issuance\n- **credentials/**: Certificate distribution and management\n\n### Service Registry Integration with Kubernetes\n\nThe service registry is the bridge between Kubernetes state and Istio configuration:\n\n1. **Kubernetes Controller** (serviceregistry/kube/controller/controller.go)\n   - Watches Kubernetes Service, Endpoints, and Pod objects\n   - Normalizes K8s concepts into Istio's abstract Service model\n   - Triggers push events when services or endpoints change\n\n2. **Service Model** (model/service.go)\n   - Abstract representation of a service (hostname, ports, endpoints)\n   - Platform-independent - works with K8s, ServiceEntry, etc.\n\n3. **Configuration Updates**\n   - When a Service or Endpoint changes, the registry notifies\n   - This triggers a PushRequest with reason `ServiceUpdate`\n   - The configuration generators use the updated registry to build new xDS resources\n\n**Example**: When you deploy a new pod in Kubernetes:\n- API server creates an Endpoint object\n- Controller watches Endpoints API\n- Controller triggers `ServiceUpdate` PushRequest\n- EDS generator reads updated endpoints\n- xDS push sent to all proxies with new endpoints\n\n---\n\n## First Contribution Workflow\n\n### Finding a Good First Issue\n\n1. Visit the [Istio GitHub Issues page](https://github.com/istio/istio/issues)\n2. Filter by label `kind/feature` or `kind/bug`\n3. Look for issues with `good-first-issue` label\n4. Priority levels: P0 (critical), P1 (important), P2 (nice-to-have)\n\n### Setting Up Your Fork\n\n```bash\n# Fork the repository on GitHub (click Fork button)\n\n# Clone your fork\ngit clone https://github.com/YOUR_USERNAME/istio.git\ncd istio\n\n# Add upstream remote for syncing\ngit remote add upstream https://github.com/istio/istio.git\n\n# Create a feature branch\ngit checkout -b my-feature-branch\n```\n\n### Making Code Changes\n\n#### Understanding the Code\n\nBefore making changes, understand the call path:\n1. Identify which component(s) your change affects (Pilot, Citadel, networking, etc.)\n2. Locate the relevant source files in that component\n3. Use `grep` or IDE search to find all callers/usages\n4. Read the tests to understand expected behavior\n\n#### Writing Your Change\n\n1. Make minimal, focused changes to address the issue\n2. Don't refactor surrounding code unless necessary\n3. Add comments only for non-obvious logic\n4. Follow existing code style in the file\n\n#### Running Tests Locally\n\n**For the files you changed**:\n```bash\n# Find all affected packages\n# Example: if you edited pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go\nPKG=./pilot/pkg/xds/... make test\n\n# Or be more specific\ngo test ./pilot/pkg/xds -v -race\n```\n\n**Write unit tests for new functionality**:\n```go\n// In discovery_test.go\nfunc TestMyNewFeature(t *testing.T) {\n    // Setup\n    // Act\n    // Assert\n}\n```\n\n**Run pre-commit checks** (required before submitting):\n```bash\nmake precommit\n```\n\nThis will:\n- Auto-format code with `gofmt` and `goimports`\n- Run linters (go vet, copyright headers, shell scripts, etc.)\n- Check for common mistakes\n\n### Creating a Pull Request\n\n1. **Commit your changes**:\n```bash\ngit add .\ngit commit -m \"Brief description of change\n\nLonger explanation if needed. Reference issue: #12345\"\n```\n\n2. **Push to your fork**:\n```bash\ngit push origin my-feature-branch\n```\n\n3. **Create PR on GitHub**:\n   - Title: Be concise and descriptive\n   - Description: Explain what and why (the how is in the code)\n   - Link issue: \"Fixes #12345\" or \"Related to #12345\"\n\n4. **PR Requirements and CI Gates**:\n   - [ ] All tests pass (automated via GitHub Actions)\n   - [ ] At least 2 approvals from maintainers\n   - [ ] Code review comments addressed\n   - [ ] No merge conflicts with main branch\n   - [ ] Signed CLA (Contributor License Agreement)\n\n5. **Common Reviewer Feedback**:\n   - Add/improve unit tests\n   - Simplify code or add explanatory comments\n   - Consider edge cases\n   - Match existing patterns in the codebase\n\n### PR Review Checklist\n\nBefore submitting, make sure:\n\n- [ ] `make precommit` passes without errors\n- [ ] `make test PKG=<modified-package>/... ` passes\n- [ ] No TODO comments or debug code\n- [ ] Commit message is clear and references the issue\n- [ ] Changes are minimal and focused on the issue\n- [ ] Backwards compatible (unless breaking change approved)\n\n---\n\n## Debugging and Development\n\n### Useful Make Targets\n\n```bash\n# Build without testing\nmake build\n\n# Build for Linux (for container images)\nmake build-linux\n\n# Run all tests with race detection\nmake test\n\n# Run tests for specific package\nPKG=./pilot/pkg/xds/... make test\n\n# Format code\nmake format\n\n# Run linters\nmake lint\n\n# Full pre-commit pipeline\nmake precommit\n\n# Show available targets\nmake help\n```\n\n### Debugging istiod Locally\n\n**Run istiod with debug logging**:\n```bash\nDEBUG=1 make build\n```\n\n**Access debug endpoints** (when istiod is running):\n```bash\n# View current mesh configuration\ncurl http://localhost:8080/debug/mesh\n\n# View connected proxies\ncurl http://localhost:8080/debug/connections\n\n# View current push context\ncurl http://localhost:8080/debug/pushcontext\n\n# View config for a specific proxy\ncurl http://localhost:8080/debug/config_dump?proxyID=<pod-name>.<namespace>\n```\n\n### Environment Variables for Development\n\nKey environment variables you might use:\n\n```bash\n# Go build tags\nAGENT_TAGS=agent,disable_pgv    # For lightweight agents\nSTANDARD_TAGS=vtprotobuf        # For full features\n\n# Build output\nTARGET_OUT=./out/linux          # Where binaries are placed\n\n# Istio config\nISTIO_NAMESPACE=istio-system\n```\n\n### Using the Test Utilities\n\nThe codebase includes excellent test utilities:\n\n**pilot/test/xds/fake.go**:\n- FakeDiscoveryServer: Mock xDS server for testing\n- Helps test proxy configuration without running full istiod\n\n**pilot/test/xdstest/extract.go**:\n- Extract listeners, clusters, routes from xDS resources\n- Validate xDS response structure\n\n**Example test**:\n```go\nimport \"istio.io/istio/pilot/test/xds\"\n\nfunc TestMyChange(t *testing.T) {\n    ds := xds.NewFakeDiscoveryServer(t, xds.FakeOptions{})\n    defer ds.Cleanup()\n\n    // Test configuration generation\n    proxy := &model.Proxy{ID: \"pod.namespace\"}\n    clusters := ds.Clusters(proxy)\n\n    // Assert clusters are correct\n    if len(clusters) == 0 {\n        t.Fatal(\"Expected clusters\")\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Key Resources\n\n### Official Documentation\n- [Istio Architecture](https://istio.io/latest/docs/concepts/what-is-istio/)\n- [Istio Developer's This guide will help you understand the control plane architecture, set up your development environment, and make your first contribution.\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [Build Prerequisites](#build-prerequisites)\n2. [Architecture Overview](#architecture-overview)\n3. [First Contribution Workflow](#first-contribution-workflow)\n4. [Debugging and Development](#debugging-and-development)\n5. [Key Resources](#key-resources)\n\n---\n\n## Build Prerequisites\n\n### System Requirements\n\n**Go Version**: 1.25.0 or later (as specified in `go.mod`)\n\nVerify your Go installation:\n```bash\ngo version\n```\n\n### Environment Setup\n\n**Clone the Repository** (with all submodules):\n```bash\ngit clone --recurse-submodules https://github.com/istio/istio.git\ncd istio\n```\n\nIf you've already cloned without submodules, initialize them:\n```bash\ngit submodule update --init --recursive\n```\n\n### Build System\n\nIstio uses a Makefile-based build system with two modes:\n\n#### Option 1: Local Build (Recommended for Development)\n\n```bash\nmake build\n```\n\nThis compiles binaries directly on your machine. You'll need:\n- Go toolchain\n- Standard build tools (gcc, make)\n\n#### Option 2: Containerized Build\n\nFor a completely isolated environment (fewer system dependencies):\n```bash\nBUILD_WITH_CONTAINER=1 make build\n```\n\nThis uses Docker to build everything in a consistent container environment. Requires Docker to be installed.\n\n### Core Binaries\n\nThe main control plane binaries built by the system are:\n\n- **`pilot-discovery`**: The core Istio discovery server, handles xDS protocol and configuration distribution\n  - Location: `./pilot/cmd/pilot-discovery`\n  - Built target: `$GOBIN/pilot-discovery`\n\n- **`pilot-agent`**: Sidecar agent that runs in each Envoy pod, manages local configuration\n  - Location: `./pilot/cmd/pilot-agent`\n  - Built target: `$GOBIN/pilot-agent`\n\n- **`istioctl`**: CLI tool for debugging and managing Istio\n  - Location: `./istioctl/cmd/istioctl`\n  - Built target: `$GOBIN/istioctl`\n\nTo build individual binaries:\n```bash\nmake pilot-discovery\nmake pilot-agent\nmake istioctl\n```\n\n### Running Tests\n\n**Unit Tests with Race Detection** (recommended):\n```bash\nmake test\n```\n\nThis runs: `go test ./... -race -tags=assert`\n\n**Run Tests for Specific Packages**:\n```bash\n# Test only the pilot package\nPKG=./pilot/... make test\n\n# Test only xDS discovery server\nPKG=./pilot/pkg/xds/... make test\n```\n\n**Run Benchmarks**:\n```bash\nmake benchtest\n```\n\n### Pre-commit Checks\n\nBefore submitting a PR, run the complete pre-commit pipeline:\n```bash\nmake precommit\n```\n\nThis runs:\n- `make fmt` - Code formatting (gofmt, goimports)\n- `make lint` - Linting (go vet, copyright banners, scripts, YAML, markdown, etc.)\n- `make tidy-go` - Dependency management\n\n**Just formatting**:\n```bash\nmake format\n```\n\n---\n\n## Architecture Overview\n\n### Control Plane Components\n\nIstio's control plane (istiod) is a single unified binary that merges three historical components:\n\n1. **Pilot** - Service discovery and traffic management\n   - Watches Kubernetes Services and ServiceEntry resources\n   - Generates xDS configuration for Envoy proxies\n   - Implements traffic policies (routing, load balancing, retries)\n\n2. **Citadel** - Certificate Authority and Identity Management\n   - Issues and manages mTLS certificates for workloads\n   - Provides certificate rotation and distribution\n   - Manages certificate revocation\n\n3. **Galley** - Configuration validation and distribution\n   - Validates Istio CRDs and Kubernetes resources\n   - Distributes validated configurations to other components\n\n### xDS Protocol: Configuration Distribution\n\nThe **xDS API** is the core protocol by which istiod pushes configuration to Envoy proxies. It consists of four main resource types:\n\n- **CDS** (Cluster Discovery Service): Defines upstream services as \"clusters\"\n  - Each cluster represents a service that traffic can be sent to\n  - Includes load balancing policies and health checks\n  - Generated by: `pilot/pkg/xds/cds.go`\n\n- **EDS** (Endpoint Discovery Service): Lists IP addresses for each cluster\n  - Provides the actual endpoints (pods) behind each service\n  - Updated when pods start/stop or change state\n  - Generated by: `pilot/pkg/xds/eds.go`\n\n- **LDS** (Listener Discovery Service): Defines listening sockets on the proxy\n  - Specifies ports and protocols the Envoy proxy should listen on\n  - Configures filter chains for different traffic types\n  - Generated by: `pilot/pkg/xds/lds.go`\n\n- **RDS** (Route Discovery Service): Defines routing rules\n  - Specifies how to route traffic between services\n  - Implements VirtualService, DestinationRule, and traffic policies\n  - Generated by: `pilot/pkg/xds/rds.go`\n\n### Data Flow: Service Discovery to xDS Push\n\nHere's the complete end-to-end flow when a new service is discovered:\n\n```\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ 1. SERVICE REGISTRATION                                         │\n│    Kubernetes API Server creates a Service object               │\n└────────────────────┬────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n                     │\n                     ▼\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ 2. SERVICE DISCOVERY                                            │\n│    ServiceRegistry (pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/)                │\n│    - KubeRegistry watches Kubernetes Services                  │\n│    - ServiceEntryRegistry watches ServiceEntry CRDs            │\n│    - AggregateRegistry combines multiple registries            │\n│                                                                 │\n│    Key files:                                                  │\n│    - serviceregistry/kube/controller/controller.go              │\n│    - serviceregistry/serviceentry/controller.go                │\n│    - serviceregistry/aggregate/controller.go                   │\n└────────────────────┬────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n                     │\n                     ▼\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ 3. CONFIGURATION UPDATE TRIGGER                                 │\n│    ServiceDiscovery emits event → PushRequest created           │\n│    Request queued in DiscoveryServer.pushChannel               │\n│                                                                 │\n│    Key files:                                                  │\n│    - xds/discovery.go (DiscoveryServer.push handler)           │\n│    - model/push.go (PushRequest/PushContext)                   │\n└────────────────────┬────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n                     │\n                     ▼\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ 4. DEBOUNCING & CONTEXT INITIALIZATION                         │\n│    Multiple events batched for efficiency                       │\n│    initPushContext() builds new model.PushContext with:        │\n│    - Current service registry state                            │\n│    - Mesh configuration                                        │\n│    - All defined VirtualServices and DestinationRules         │\n│    - Security policies                                         │\n│                                                                 │\n│    Key files:                                                  │\n│    - model/pushcontext.go (PushContext initialization)         │\n│    - xds/discovery.go:initPushContext()                       │\n└────────────────────┬────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n                     │\n                     ▼\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ 5. CONFIGURATION GENERATION                                     │\n│    For each connected proxy, generators build xDS resources:   │\n│                                                                 │\n│    CDS Generator (xds/cds.go)                                  │\n│    → Calls ConfigGenerator.BuildClusters()                     │\n│    → Creates Cluster resources for all services                │\n│                                                                 │\n│    EDS Generator (xds/eds.go)                                  │\n│    → Calls ConfigGenerator.BuildEndpoints()                    │\n│    → Creates ClusterLoadAssignment for each cluster            │\n│    → Reads from EndpointIndex (service discovery)              │\n│                                                                 │\n│    LDS Generator (xds/lds.go)                                  │\n│    → Calls ConfigGenerator.BuildListeners()                    │\n│    → Creates Listener resources on proxy's ports               │\n│                                                                 │\n│    RDS Generator (xds/rds.go)                                  │\n│    → Calls ConfigGenerator.BuildRoutes()                       │\n│    → Creates RouteConfiguration with VirtualService rules     │\n│                                                                 │\n│    Key files:                                                  │\n│    - pilot/pkg/networking/core/configgen.go (ConfigGenerator) │\n│    - pilot/pkg/xds/v3/ (xDS generators)                       │\n└────────────────────┬────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n                     │\n                     ▼\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ 6. XDS PUSH TO PROXIES                                          │\n│    DiscoveryServer.AdsPushAll() or AdsPush()                   │\n│    sends update via gRPC to all connected Envoy proxies        │\n│                                                                 │\n│    Protocols:                                                  │\n│    - ADS (Aggregated Discovery Service): Single gRPC stream    │\n│    - Delta xDS: Incremental updates                            │\n│                                                                 │\n│    Key files:                                                  │\n│    - xds/ads.go (ADS protocol)                                 │\n│    - xds/delta.go (Delta xDS)                                  │\n│    - xds/discovery.go (Push implementation)                    │\n└────────────────────┬────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n                     │\n                     ▼\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ 7. PROXY APPLICATION                                            │\n│    Envoy proxy receives xDS update                             │\n│    → Updates local routing configuration                       │\n│    → Applies new clusters, endpoints, listeners, routes        │\n│    → Traffic now flows according to new configuration          │\n└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n### Key Packages and Their Responsibilities\n\n#### `pilot/pkg/xds/` - xDS Protocol Implementation\n- **discovery.go**: Core DiscoveryServer that manages gRPC connections and pushes\n- **ads.go**: ADS (Aggregated Discovery Service) protocol handler\n- **delta.go**: Delta xDS incremental update handler\n- **cds.go, eds.go, lds.go, rds.go**: Individual xDS resource generators\n- **monitoring.go**: Metrics for push operations and timing\n\n**Entry point**: `DiscoveryServer` struct in discovery.go:64\n\n#### `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/` - Service Discovery\nMultiple registry implementations:\n- **kube/controller/**: Kubernetes service discovery (watches K8s API)\n- **serviceentry/**: ServiceEntry resource discovery\n- **aggregate/**: Combines multiple registries\n\n**Key interface**: `Instance` interface for service registries\n\n#### `pilot/pkg/bootstrap/` - Server Initialization\n- **server.go**: Main Server struct (line 105) that orchestrates istiod startup\n- **servicecontroller.go**: Initializes all service registries\n- **configcontroller.go**: Sets up configuration watchers for CRDs\n- **discovery.go**: Initializes xDS generators\n- **istio_ca.go**: Certificate Authority initialization\n- **mesh.go**: Mesh configuration loading\n\n#### `pilot/pkg/model/` - Core Data Models\n- **environment.go**: Global Environment with ServiceDiscovery, ConfigStore\n- **push.go**: PushContext and PushRequest (configuration version)\n- **proxy.go**: Proxy model representing an Envoy instance\n\n#### `pilot/pkg/networking/` - Configuration Generation\n- **core/configgen.go**: ConfigGenerator interface for building xDS resources\n- **core/v1alpha3/**: Legacy traffic management implementation\n- **security/authz/**: Authorization policy generation\n- **policy/**: Traffic policy implementation\n\n#### `security/pkg/` - Certificate Management\n- **pki/**: Private key infrastructure and CA operations\n- **server/ca/**: CA server for certificate issuance\n- **credentials/**: Certificate distribution and management\n\n### Service Registry Integration with Kubernetes\n\nThe service registry is the bridge between Kubernetes state and Istio configuration:\n\n1. **Kubernetes Controller** (serviceregistry/kube/controller/controller.go)\n   - Watches Kubernetes Service, Endpoints, and Pod objects\n   - Normalizes K8s concepts into Istio's abstract Service model\n   - Triggers push events when services or endpoints change\n\n2. **Service Model** (model/service.go)\n   - Abstract representation of a service (hostname, ports, endpoints)\n   - Platform-independent - works with K8s, ServiceEntry, etc.\n\n3. **Configuration Updates**\n   - When a Service or Endpoint changes, the registry notifies\n   - This triggers a PushRequest with reason `ServiceUpdate`\n   - The configuration generators use the updated registry to build new xDS resources\n\n**Example**: When you deploy a new pod in Kubernetes:\n- API server creates an Endpoint object\n- Controller watches Endpoints API\n- Controller triggers `ServiceUpdate` PushRequest\n- EDS generator reads updated endpoints\n- xDS push sent to all proxies with new endpoints\n\n---\n\n## First Contribution Workflow\n\n### Finding a Good First Issue\n\n1. Visit the [Istio GitHub Issues page](https://github.com/istio/istio/issues)\n2. Filter by label `kind/feature` or `kind/bug`\n3. Look for issues with `good-first-issue` label\n4. Priority levels: P0 (critical), P1 (important), P2 (nice-to-have)\n\n### Setting Up Your Fork\n\n```bash\n# Fork the repository on GitHub (click Fork button)\n\n# Clone your fork\ngit clone https://github.com/YOUR_USERNAME/istio.git\ncd istio\n\n# Add upstream remote for syncing\ngit remote add upstream https://github.com/istio/istio.git\n\n# Create a feature branch\ngit checkout -b my-feature-branch\n```\n\n### Making Code Changes\n\n#### Understanding the Code\n\nBefore making changes, understand the call path:\n1. Identify which component(s) your change affects (Pilot, Citadel, networking, etc.)\n2. Locate the relevant source files in that component\n3. Use `grep` or IDE search to find all callers/usages\n4. Read the tests to understand expected behavior\n\n#### Writing Your Change\n\n1. Make minimal, focused changes to address the issue\n2. Don't refactor surrounding code unless necessary\n3. Add comments only for non-obvious logic\n4. Follow existing code style in the file\n\n#### Running Tests Locally\n\n**For the files you changed**:\n```bash\n# Find all affected packages\n# Example: if you edited pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go\nPKG=./pilot/pkg/xds/... make test\n\n# Or be more specific\ngo test ./pilot/pkg/xds -v -race\n```\n\n**Write unit tests for new functionality**:\n```go\n// In discovery_test.go\nfunc TestMyNewFeature(t *testing.T) {\n    // Setup\n    // Act\n    // Assert\n}\n```\n\n**Run pre-commit checks** (required before submitting):\n```bash\nmake precommit\n```\n\nThis will:\n- Auto-format code with `gofmt` and `goimports`\n- Run linters (go vet, copyright headers, shell scripts, etc.)\n- Check for common mistakes\n\n### Creating a Pull Request\n\n1. **Commit your changes**:\n```bash\ngit add .\ngit commit -m \"Brief description of change\n\nLonger explanation if needed. Reference issue: #12345\"\n```\n\n2. **Push to your fork**:\n```bash\ngit push origin my-feature-branch\n```\n\n3. **Create PR on GitHub**:\n   - Title: Be concise and descriptive\n   - Description: Explain what and why (the how is in the code)\n   - Link issue: \"Fixes #12345\" or \"Related to #12345\"\n\n4. **PR Requirements and CI Gates**:\n   - [ ] All tests pass (automated via GitHub Actions)\n   - [ ] At least 2 approvals from maintainers\n   - [ ] Code review comments addressed\n   - [ ] No merge conflicts with main branch\n   - [ ] Signed CLA (Contributor License Agreement)\n\n5. **Common Reviewer Feedback**:\n   - Add/improve unit tests\n   - Simplify code or add explanatory comments\n   - Consider edge cases\n   - Match existing patterns in the codebase\n\n### PR Review Checklist\n\nBefore submitting, make sure:\n\n- [ ] `make precommit` passes without errors\n- [ ] `make test PKG=<modified-package>/... ` passes\n- [ ] No TODO comments or debug code\n- [ ] Commit message is clear and references the issue\n- [ ] Changes are minimal and focused on the issue\n- [ ] Backwards compatible (unless breaking change approved)\n\n---\n\n## Debugging and Development\n\n### Useful Make Targets\n\n```bash\n# Build without testing\nmake build\n\n# Build for Linux (for container images)\nmake build-linux\n\n# Run all tests with race Show available targets\nmake help\n```\n\n### Debugging istiod Locally\n\n**Run istiod with debug logging**:\n```bash\nDEBUG=1 make build\n```\n\n**Access debug endpoints** (when istiod is
